## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: continuum mechanics / thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship σ(ε, T) describing material stress as a function of strain and temperature, a fundamental problem in solid mechanics where temperature typically causes thermal softening and strain causes hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': "Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity with constant modulus)"}
- {'name': 'Temperature-dependent linear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus varies linearly with temperature)'}
- {'name': 'Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood / Hollomon strain hardening)'}
- {'name': 'Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)'}
- {'name': 'Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (additive yield + hardening with thermal factor)'}
- {'name': 'Exponential thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal dependence of flow stress)'}
- {'name': 'Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating exponential hardening)'}
- {'name': 'Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with temperature effect)'}
- {'name': 'Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)'}
- {'name': 'Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive approximation)'}
- {'name': 'Rubber elasticity (neo-Hookean type): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**3) * (c2 + c3 * T) (entropic elasticity, stress proportional to T)'}
- {'name': 'Entropic spring: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (ideal rubber/entropic elasticity where modulus is proportional to temperature)'}
- {'name': 'Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)'}
- {'name': 'Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/sinh-type constitutive model)'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear stress-strain at small ε transitioning to sublinear (hardening saturation) at large ε → power-law ε**c with c<1, or saturating forms like 1-exp(-c*ε)
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor that decreases with T, such as (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T)
- Entropic elasticity in polymers/rubbers → stress proportional to T (modulus increases with temperature), σ ~ c*T*f(ε)
- Yield stress plus hardening → additive structure: σ = σ_y + f(ε), where σ_y may depend on T
- Phase transitions or sudden property changes with temperature → sigmoidal T-dependence, e.g., 1/(1+exp(c*(T-T_c)))
- Strain hardening rate decreasing with strain → concave stress-strain curve, captured by ε**c (c<1) or log(1+c*ε)
- Nonlinear elasticity with odd symmetry in strain → odd polynomial or sinh(c*ε) forms
- Coupled thermo-mechanical response → product form f(ε)*g(T) as separable approximation of constitutive law
